    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="d6bb0a0aaf0747e1b59a96eda648a08a">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'cdd31f3b-1ccb-4dfa-86a2-e4375daea20a'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d148834734" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Achieving multi-sodium storage and high operating voltage is key to boosting energy density of NASICON-type materials. However, the activation of more redox couples is usually accompanied by asymmetric and irreversible electrochemical reactions, thus causing fast capacity fading. To address this issue, a medium-entropy concept is proposed, and a novel medium-entropy Na<sub>3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>V<sub>2/3</sub>Ti<sub>2/3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C@CNTs (ME-NMVTP) cathode is designed. The as-prepared ME-NMVTP achieves a successive redox reaction, delivering a highly reversible specific capacity of 147.9&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> together with a long-term lifespan of 1000 cycles at 500&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> (capacity retention of 88.3%), which is superior to low-entropy cathodes such as Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C@CNTs (LE-NMVP) and Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C@CNTs (LE-NMTP). Moreover, benefiting from the entropy effect, solid-solution and biphasic reactions with reversible structure evolution and small volume change are achieved during the multi-sodium storage process. First-principles calculation and kinetic analysis results affirm the enhanced electronic conductivity and facilitated Na<sup>+</sup> migration of the ME-NMVTP cathode derived from the synergistic effect of the three transition-metal elementals in a medium-entropy crystalline state. The strategy of engineering medium-entropy to construct cathodes with superior performance is expected to be widely applicable to other electrode materials.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202302046-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202302046-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>The rapid development of renewable energy resources is stimulating a high demand for cost-efficient large-scale energy storage systems (ESSs).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0001_R_d148834726e420" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Energy Environ. Sci.">1</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0002_R_d148834726e420" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Renewable Sustainable Energy Rev.">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Although lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have made great strides in various fields, such as portable electronic devices and electric vehicles, their suitability for large-scale EESs is still somewhat controversial due to the scarcity and uneven distribution of lithium resources.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0003_R_d148834726e425" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Mater. Today">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In this context, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered a promising option for EESs because of the low cost, abundant resources of sodium, and its similar working mechanism to LIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0004_R_d148834726e430" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - iScience">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> SIBs have garnered significant experience regarding theoretical research and practical applications.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0005_R_d148834726e436" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Nat. Commun.">5</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0006_R_d148834726e436" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Developing high-performance cathodes for SIBs, however, is still a great challenge, because it is necessary to solve multiple interrelated issues including sluggish reaction kinetics, unstable crystal structure, etc.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0007_R_d148834726e441" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Through multiple comparisons, polyanionic compounds, especially Na superionic conductor (NASICON) materials, will hold a predominant place in large-scale EESs due to their open 3D framework structure and thereby facilitated Na<sup>+</sup> mobility.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0008_R_d148834726e449" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0009_R_d148834726e449" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - J. Mater. Chem. A">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Typically, NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) can deliver a reversible capacity of over 110&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> with an output voltage of 3.4&nbsp;V and high cycling stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0010_R_d148834726e465" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the primary concerns and obstacles are how to boost energy density and reduce materials cost, thus improving competitiveness in mass production and commercial application.</p>
         
         <p>In the quest for ideal cathodes, researchers attempted to introduce different active transition-metal (TM) centers into NASICON materials to regulate the mean operating voltage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0011_R_d148834726e473" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Energy Storage Mater.">11</a>-<a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0013_R_d148834726e473" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - J. Electroanal. Chem.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Manganese seems to be an attractive element because the reversible redox reaction involved in Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> couples (3.6&nbsp;V) has been proposed and investigated in the NASICON compounds for SIBs, Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, Na<sub>3</sub>MnZr(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, and Na<sub>4</sub>MnCr(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>. etc.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0014_R_d148834726e502" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Nano Energy">14</a>-<a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0016_R_d148834726e502" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Small">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Activation of Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> redox can achieve high voltage and introduction of Mn can reduce material cost. However, if the electrochemical reaction of NASICON cathodes is limited to 2 per formula (one electron per TM), their energy density is still difficult to meet the actual demand. For this reason, exploring NASICON-type cathodes with multielectron redox reactions has become a hot point. Zhu et&nbsp;al. reported a Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> material with three-electron reaction (Ti<sup>3+</sup>/<sup>4+</sup> and Mn<sup>2+</sup>/<sup>4+</sup> redox couples), which delivers a high specific capacity of 160&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2&nbsp;C.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0017_R_d148834726e529" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Energy Mater.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Na<sub>4</sub>MnCr(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> would enable 2.35 Na<sup>+</sup> or 3 Na<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalation during discharge utilizing high-voltage Mn<sup>2+</sup>/<sup>3+</sup>, Mn<sup>3+</sup>/<sup>4+</sup>, and Cr<sup>3+</sup>/<sup>4+</sup> TM redox.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0018_R_d148834726e558" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Adv. Energy Mater.">18</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0019_R_d148834726e558" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Adv. Mater.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Afterward, the electrochemical behaviors of NASICON-type Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>1.5</sub>Cr<sub>0.5</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>2</sub>VTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> with multielectron redox reactions have been investigated.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0020_R_d148834726e581" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">20</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0021_R_d148834726e581" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Chem. Eng. J.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The multielectron redox reactions effectively endow NASICON-type cathodes with high specific capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0022_R_d148834726e586" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Unfortunately, a series of issues including significant capacity decay and irreversible phase transition evolution under high voltage operation would spontaneously occur.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0023_R_d148834726e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Small Methods">23</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0024_R_d148834726e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Mater.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the case of a typical Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> material, both Mn and V exhibit drastic local distortions under high voltage, leading to irreversible electrochemical reactions (monoclinic phase→rhombohedral phase).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0024_R_d148834726e603" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Mater.">24</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0025_R_d148834726e603" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Hence, the realization of the highly reversible multielectron redox reactions within the NASICON framework is vital.</p>
         
         <p>In recent years, the regulation of conformational entropy has drawn increasing interest, mainly because it may lead to a greater number of possible interaction combinations by increasing entropy.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0026_R_d148834726e612" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Mater.">26</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0027_R_d148834726e612" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Small">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As a result, various functional/structural materials exhibit unique properties for energy storage. The evolved high-entropy phosphate cathodes, Na<sub>3.4</sub>Fe<sub>0.4</sub>Mn<sub>0.4</sub>V<sub>0.4</sub>Cr<sub>0.4</sub>Ti<sub>0.4</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>3</sub>VAl<sub>0.2</sub>Cr<sub>0.2</sub>Fe<sub>0.2</sub>In<sub>0.2</sub>Ga<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, have demonstrated that the high-entropy effect can restrain the structural degradation caused by the electrochemical cycling under the high voltage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0028_R_d148834726e652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Sci.">28</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0029_R_d148834726e652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Energy Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, TM sites in high-entropy phosphate materials are composed of five or more elements, which inevitably induce lattice distortion due to differences in size and bond energy between elements. Severe lattice distortion may render the crystal structure unsustainable, resulting in lattice collapse, so the controlled synthesis of some high-entropy materials is very difficult. Inspired by these cases, herein, we computationally designed and experimentally synthesized a novel medium-entropy NASICON-type compound Na<sub>3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>V<sub>2/3</sub>Ti<sub>2/3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C@CNTs (ME-NMVTP), which could strengthen the structural stability and achieve reversible 2.7 Na<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalation. The advantageous medium-entropy effect in ME-NMVTP enhances electronic and ionic diffusion kinetic, greatly improving sodium storage capacity in comparison to low-entropy cathodes. Specifically, the ME-NMVTP exhibits a reversible capacity of 147.9&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> and a long cycling lifespan of 88.3% retention after 1000 cycles at 500&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>. The sodium storage mechanism involved in reaction plateau, capacity contribution, kinetic analysis, structure revolution, etc. has been comprehensively and systemically investigated. In addition, when coupled with the hard carbon anode, the full cells also display promising electrochemical performance.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202302046-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202302046-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>These NASICON materials with different concentrations of TM species were synthesized by sol–gel method. According to the definition derived from statistical thermodynamics (ΔS<sub>conf</sub> = −R(<span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/08431af9-97e5-4881-b03a-a341d1424d0a/aenm202302046-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202302046:aenm202302046-math-0001" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202302046-math-0001.png">
               <semantics>
                  <mrow>
                     <munderover>
                        <mo>∑</mo>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>i</mi>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mo>=</mo>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mn>1</mn>
                        </mrow>
                        <mi>n</mi>
                     </munderover>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>x</mi>
                        <mi>i</mi>
                     </msub>
                     <mi>ln</mi>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>x</mi>
                        <mi>i</mi>
                     </msub>
                  </mrow>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$\mathop \sum \limits_{i\ = \ 1}^n {x}_i{\mathrm{ln}}{x}_i$</annotation>
               </semantics></math>), <i>x<sub>i</sub></i> represents the mole fraction of the <i>i</i><sup>th</sup> TM species), the ΔS<sub>conf</sub> of LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP with double redox centers are both 0.69R, belonging to the low-entropy range (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0001">1a</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0030_R_d148834726e728" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Energy Environ. Sci.">30</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0031_R_d148834726e728" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - JOM">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The ΔS<sub>conf</sub> of ME-NMVTP with three different TM species at the cation sites is calculated to be 1.10R (medium-entropy). Significantly, the configurational entropy reaches the largest value when the mole fraction is the same for all TM species. Rietveld refinement analyses of XRD patterns for as-prepared cathodes exhibit that all three samples adopt a typical trigonal (R-3c) structure, confirming the full solubility of Mn<sup>2+</sup>, V<sup>3+</sup>, and Ti<sup>4+</sup> in the framework (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0001">1b</a>; Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0032_R_d148834726e752" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Chem. Eng. J.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> And the specific crystallographic data including lattice parameters, and atomic positions or occupations, are recorded in Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>–<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information). The difference in lattice parameters and cell volume for as-prepared cathodes is a comprehensive result of the variation of TM species and the corresponding adjusted sodium contents. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0001">1e</a>, the ME-NMVTP cathode owns a smaller cell volume as well as the cell parameter (a) in comparison with LE-cathodes, which is caused by less Na<sup>+</sup> into the lattice and the decreased proportion of the Mn<sup>2+</sup> with a larger ionic radius (r<sub>Mn</sub><sup>2+</sup> = 80 pm, r<sub>V</sub><sup>3+</sup> = 64 pm, r<sub>Ti</sub><sup>4+</sup> = 60.5 pm).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0022_R_d148834726e781" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">22</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0032_R_d148834726e781" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Chem. Eng. J.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, an increased cell parameter c could be obtained in the ME-NMVTP cathode, which is mainly attributed to the expansion caused by the enhanced electrostatic repulsion between TMO<sub>6</sub> octahedra along the c direction due to decreased Na1 occupation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0033_R_d148834726e788" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Adv. Energy Mater.">33</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0034_R_d148834726e788" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Small">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The expansion of the c-axis is expected to provide a more convenient condition for Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion. Besides, due to the relatively lower bonding force of the Na2─O bond, the occupation of Na1 declines, and that of Na2 gradually increase in the ME-NMVTP material, making it more favorable for Na<sup>+</sup> extraction and insertion than other materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0035_R_d148834726e798" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Adv. Energy Mater.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0001">1c</a> also exhibits the visualization of crystal structure and atomic occupation of ME-NMVTP via GSAS and Vesta software, where the octahedral TM sites are statistically equally occupied by Mn, V, and Ti. Na<sup>+</sup> is located in the interstitial sites formed by the corner-shared of the [Mn/V/TiO<sub>6</sub>] octahedra and [PO<sub>4</sub>] tetrahedra. And the stretching vibrations of TM─O bonds in octahedra and P─O bonds in tetrahedra were detected by FTIR results (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0001">1f</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0036_R_d148834726e816" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Mater. Chem. Front.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Particularly, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0001">1d</a> magnifies the structure of the TMO<sub>6</sub> octahedron in as-prepared materials. The TMO<sub>6</sub> octahedron in LE-NMVP structure has serious geometric distortion or deformation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0037_R_d148834726e829" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Energy Lett.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> ME-NVTMP cathode with relatively symmetrical TMO<sub>6</sub> octahedra shows shortened average TM─O bond lengths in contrast to LE-NMTP, indicating its more covalent feature and higher structural stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0037_R_d148834726e836" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Energy Lett.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202302046-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/56526547-185d-41c2-b25f-7d330814492b/aenm202302046-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/56526547-185d-41c2-b25f-7d330814492b/aenm202302046-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/b1d15435-e0de-4acc-880c-c6fb3fc5954e/aenm202302046-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/56526547-185d-41c2-b25f-7d330814492b/aenm202302046-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202302046-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202302046" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Comparison of the configurational entropy of ME-NMVTP with other cathodes in references. b,c) Rietveld refinement profile and crystal structure of the ME-NMVTP cathode. d) The elaborate amplification of TMO<sub>6</sub> octahedra. e,f) The histograms of lattice parameters and FTIR curves of ME-NMVTP, LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP cathodes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To investigate the surface chemical compositions and oxidation states of the material, X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) results of ME-NMVTP, LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP materials were contrasted. Taking ME-NMVTP as an example, the presence of Na, Mn, V, Ti, P, O, and C elements was clearly observed from the full spectrum (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0002">2a</a> shows five fitted peaks in the high-resolution Mn 2p XPS spectrum, among which the peaks at 641.25&nbsp;eV (Mn 2p3/2) and 653.44&nbsp;eV (Mn 2p1/2) correspond to Mn<sup>2+</sup> species, and the peaks at 642.72&nbsp;eV (Mn 2p3/2) and 654.69&nbsp;eV (Mn 2p1/2) correspond to Mn<sup>3+</sup> species.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0035_R_d148834726e879" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Adv. Energy Mater.">35</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0038_R_d148834726e879" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - J. Mater. Chem. A">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> While V exists in the form of trivalent in ME-NMVTP and LE-NMVP cathodes, specifically, the high-resolution V 2p XPS spectra are split into two peaks centered at ≈517.22 and 523.96&nbsp;eV (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0002">2b</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4a</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0039_R_d148834726e890" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Small">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> And the Ti also presents a mixed valence state as the Mn does (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0002">2c</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4b</a>, Supporting Information). Among them, the stronger peaks at 460.46 and 466.12&nbsp;eV are characteristic peaks of Ti<sup>4+</sup>, and the weaker peaks at 459.11 and 464.77&nbsp;eV are characteristic peaks of Ti<sup>3+</sup>, determining that the as-prepared cathodes are mainly Ti<sup>4+</sup>, with a relatively small amount of Ti<sup>3+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0022_R_d148834726e911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">22</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0028_R_d148834726e911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Sci.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The molar concentrations of three TM elements in ME-NMVTP are similar as confirmed by inductively coupled plasma optical emission spectroscopy (ICP), which agrees well with the designed composition ratios within an acceptable range of error (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0002">2d</a>). Therefore, the mixed valence states of Mn and Ti are associated with the oxidation process occurring in the local surface region upon exposure to air, which is consistent with previous findings.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0040_R_d148834726e919" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Nano Res.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202302046-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4a20b43e-a808-4b25-b0cf-d24243718c82/aenm202302046-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/4a20b43e-a808-4b25-b0cf-d24243718c82/aenm202302046-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/3bacd411-0863-41a1-b000-4f645ceed6d7/aenm202302046-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4a20b43e-a808-4b25-b0cf-d24243718c82/aenm202302046-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202302046-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202302046" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a–c) High-resolution Mn 2p, V 2p and Ti 2p XPS spectrum of ME-NMVTP cathode. d) The atomic ratio of three TM elements in ME-NMVTP. e–h) TEM, HRTEM images and TEM–EDS mappings of ME-NMVTP cathode.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information) shows that the ME-NMVTP has polyhedral-shaped particle morphology with a micrometer-scale size distribution, which is uniformly wrapped by interpenetrating CNTs. As further indicated by the TEM image (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0002">2e</a>), the large particles are assembled by a large number of nanoparticles. Moreover, a thin amorphous carbon layer is observed to tightly coat the ME-NMVTP surface due to the pyrolysis of organic precursors, which can be connected with CNTs to enable fast electronic migration with 3D pathways (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0002">2f</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0041_R_d148834726e954" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) test shows that the carbon amount is ≈10% (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information). The nature of carbon was characterized by Raman spectra. As seen in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information), two discernable peaks at 1335 and 1596 cm<sup>−1</sup> are related to the D-band and the G-band of carbon framework. The I<sub>D</sub>/I<sub>G</sub> value of ME-NMVTP cathode is &lt;1, which indicates a higher graphitization degree, resulting in an enhanced electronic conductivity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0042_R_d148834726e973" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> And the ME-NMVTP exhibits a high specific surface area (32.5 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>) and sufficient mesoporous (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information). In addition, the atomic structure of ME-NMVTP was further observed by HRTEM (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0002">2g</a>). The well-defined lattice fringes with spacing of 6.2 Å point to the (012) plane of the trigonal NASICON structure. TEM-based energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) mappings also demonstrate that each element is evenly distributed throughout the entire particle (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0002">2h</a>). As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a> (Supporting Information), the morphology of LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP is similar to that of ME-NMVTP, both of which are aggregated by primary nanoparticles. Besides the introduction of continuous and complete carbon skeleton, they show a uniform distribution of Na, TM (M = Mn, V, or Ti), P, and O elements at a given resolution.</p>
         
         <p>Na-ion half cells were tested to evaluate the influence of medium-entropy effect on the electrochemical performance. <b>Figures</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0003">3a–c</a> provide the galvanostatic charge/discharge (GCD) curves and cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of ME-NMVTP, LE-NMVP, and LE-NMTP cathodes between 1.5 and 4.3&nbsp;V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) at 20&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, clearly conveying information about the potential platform, capacity delivery, etc. As seen, LE-NMVP displays a discharge capacity of 127.0&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> based on the redox of V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup> and Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0043_R_d148834726e1020" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Nano Energy">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Due to the small potential difference, the GCD curves of LE-NMVP deliver an extended plateau from 3.2 to 3.7&nbsp;V. Of note, the poor coincidence is found in the CV curves of the LE-NMVP. In particular, the oxidation peaks located at 3.54, 3.66, and 3.95&nbsp;V transform into a wide peak in the subsequent cycles. And Coulombic efficiency is significantly lower than the other two cathodes. These phenomena are related to the serious structural distortion and irreversible capacity loss of LE-NMVP caused by the further electrochemical activity of V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup> redox couple (≈3.95&nbsp;V).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0024_R_d148834726e1030" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Mater.">24</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0037_R_d148834726e1030" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Energy Lett.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> While LE-NMTP shows three pairs of obvious discharge potential plateaus, corresponding to the redox couples of Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup> (≈2.1&nbsp;V, 2.4&nbsp;V) and Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup> (≈4.0&nbsp;V).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0017_R_d148834726e1044" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Energy Mater.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Its initial discharge capacity is close to 139.0&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. Remarkably, the ME-NMVTP delivers a reversible capacity reaching 158.6&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, which is much higher than that of LE-NMVP, and LE-NMTP. CV curves show there are four pairs of redox potentials at about 1.75/1.50, 2.31/1.99, 3.55/3.32, and 4.02/3.94&nbsp;V, in accordance with the GCD results. Since the redox potentials of Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> and Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup> are close to those of V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup> and V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup>, these redox peaks should be attributed to the V<sup>2+</sup>/V<sup>3+</sup>, Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup>, V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup>, Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup>, V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup>, and Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup> redox, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0022_R_d148834726e1097" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">22</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0032_R_d148834726e1097" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Chem. Eng. J.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Overall, the ME-NMVTP cathode has superior energy density because of the combination of high capacity and high average operating potential.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202302046-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d92ea0dd-816c-44e1-a098-b47e894524cd/aenm202302046-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/d92ea0dd-816c-44e1-a098-b47e894524cd/aenm202302046-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/87b088c7-558f-4568-a18c-89f42a6eb63e/aenm202302046-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/d92ea0dd-816c-44e1-a098-b47e894524cd/aenm202302046-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202302046-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202302046" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">GCD and CV curves of a) ME-NMVTP, b) LE-NMVP, and c) LE-NMTP cathodes. Cycling performance of as-prepared cathodes at d) 50 and g) 500&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>. e) Capacity contribution and Coulombic efficiency of as-prepared cathodes calculated from (d). f) Rate performance and h) the corresponding GCD curves of ME-NMVTP from 20 to 5000&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Cycling performance of ME-NMVTP, LE-NMVP, and LE-NMTP cathodes were evaluated (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0003">3d</a>). The ME-NMVTP shows an initial discharge capacity of 147.9&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, which is superior to those of LE-NMVP (109.5&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>), and LE-NMTP (134.5&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>). After 150 cycles, a discharge capacity of ≈129.5&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> is obtained, corresponding to 87.6% of capacity retention. In contrast, LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP cathodes exhibit obvious capacity attenuation. Based on this discharge data, Coulombic efficiency and capacity contribution highlighted with diverse colors are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0003">3e</a>. The ME-NMVTP offers a more balanced specific capacity in the different voltage regions and better cycling stability in the high-voltage region. The Coulombic efficiency of the second cycle is 99.0%, far exceeding those of LE-NMVP (91.4%), and LE-NMTP (96.7%). Then, the extremer electrochemical test is arranged for all as-prepared cathodes at 500&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> for several weeks of running. The initial capacity of ME-NMVTP is 121.5&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, which is slightly reduced to 107.3&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles with a capacity retention of 88.3% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0003">3g</a>). As summarized in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information), ME-NMVTP exhibits fairly good performance in comparison with previously reported NASICON structure electrodes. However, for the LE-NMVP cathode, its capacity falls drastically only in the small current activation phase, accompanied by a fast voltage attenuation (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). Note that LE-NMTP cathode behaves with considerable capacity retention after activation, but its low-capacity delivery and voltage output greatly weaken its competitiveness. In fact, the capacity attenuation of LE-NMTP at low current density may relate to the Jahn−Teller structural distortion of MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedron centers in the structure, which is mainly caused by the contraction or elongation of the O−Mn−O bond along the axial direction in the octahedral units.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0037_R_d148834726e1167" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Energy Lett.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, realizing multi-sodium storage within a wide test voltage window is indeed a rigorous ordeal for cathode materials. Because the cycling performance is usually involved in the structural stability of material, the structure information of the ME-NMVTP after 1000 cycles was further analyzed via SEM and XRD. The original architecture is perfectly maintained even after ultralong cycling, indicating CNTs as a steady skeleton could shape a natural barrier for ME-NMVTP (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11a</a>, Supporting Information). Except for the additional reflection peaks from the Al foil, all the other peaks are well-indexed to the trigonal ME-NMVTP phase without impurity (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11b</a>, Supporting Information). This also demonstrates the integrated/synergistic effect of Mn, V, and Ti will improve the structural stability of the crystal structure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0028_R_d148834726e1179" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Sci.">28</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0035_R_d148834726e1179" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Adv. Energy Mater.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The superiority of medium-entropy effect is further clarified by the electrochemical performance test under a consecutive periodic variation condition of current density. Compared to LE-NASICON cathode, rate capability of ME-NMVTP is obviously improved (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0003">3f</a>). More precisely, at the current densities of 20, 50, 100, 200, 500, 1000, 2000, 3000, and 5000&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, the discharge capacities are 158.6, 140.5, 130.8, 123.3, 115.0, 108.1, 89.6, 74.1, and 57.7&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, which are higher than those of LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP. And the reversible capacity of ME-NMVTP recovers to initial values after 45 cycles, manifesting that the reversible Na<sup>+</sup> storage process in ME-NMVTP is more rapid and stable. And ME-NMVTP can maintain mean discharge potential plateaus at all rates to a higher level, corresponding to smaller polarization than LE-cathodes. The difference is more pronounced at higher current density (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0003">3h</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). Such circumstances mainly originate from the entropy-driven stabilization effect, which is in agreement with the high-entropy phosphate cathodes reported.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0026_R_d148834726e1200" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Mater.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> On account of structure optimization by medium-entropy effect, the reversible capacity, cycling durability, rate performance, as well as energy density of ME-NMVTP are further improved synchronously, taking a significant step in the commercial application.</p>
         
         <p>From the perspective of electrochemical performance, the experimental results have confirmed that medium-entropy substitution (increasing the TM variety with similar molarity) is effective to optimize cathode materials. Further investigating and comparing the apparent Na<sup>+</sup> migration kinetics is key to understanding this behavioral difference in the NASICON structure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0044_R_d148834726e1210" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Chem. Eng. J.">44</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0045_R_d148834726e1210" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Energy Storage Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> There are two calculation methods, one is based on CV curves at various sweep rates (0.2–1.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>). As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0004">4a</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> (Supporting Information), the electrodes are cycled in the voltage range of 1.5–4.3&nbsp;V. Due to the enlarged polarization, the intensities and potential differences of all redox peaks increase with the increased scanning rates.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0036_R_d148834726e1227" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Mater. Chem. Front.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Plotting peak current (<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>) against the square root of the scan rates (<i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>) results in a linear relationship (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information), indicating that the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i><sub>Na</sub>) can be determined by Randles–Sevcik equation (Equation <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information), as listed in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0045_R_d148834726e1254" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Energy Storage Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Supposing that the difference in n, A, and C parameters is negligible, thus, the slopes (<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>/<i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>) also reflect apparent diffusion kinetics during redox reactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0046_R_d148834726e1266" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Alloys Compd.">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> And the slopes of ME-NMVTP corresponding to each insertion/extraction step (the three pairs of the redox peaks (O1, O2, O3, R1, R2, and R3)) are substantially greater than those of the LE-NMVP, implying that Na<sup>+</sup> diffuses faster throughout charge/discharge process (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0004">4b</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information). Analogously, galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was further performed to compare the <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub> value change of ME-NMVTP, LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP cathodes (Figure 4c; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information). The single titration curves and the calculations involved are described in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a> and Equation <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0047_R_d148834726e1292" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Nano Energy">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The ME-NMVTP displays smaller fluctuations in <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub> values within a relatively narrow range of ≈10<sup>−8</sup>–10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, surpassing the correlative values of LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP. Especially for LE-NMTP cathode, the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion rate of the high potential platform is much lower than that of other platform regions, which severely limits the overall Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics. Overall, both CV and GITT tests manifest that after the medium-entropy effect is introduced into NASICON material, the electrode kinetics are enhanced. The electrochemical reaction dynamics can be further explored by Equations <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>–<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). The log(<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>)-log(<i>v</i>) for ME-NMVTP, LE-NMVP, and LE-NMTP display a good linear relationship, where the b values of CV peaks are mainly between 0.6 and 0.8 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information), manifesting the partial pseudocapacitive effect and thus enabling the rapid reaction dynamics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0014_R_d148834726e1329" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Nano Energy">14</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0047_R_d148834726e1329" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Nano Energy">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The contribution of capacitance can be quantified by Equation <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0004">4d</a> presents the detailed pseudocapacitive fraction for ME-NMVTP at 0.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> is 92.66%, much higher than that of LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a>, Supporting Information). The proportions of capacitive contribution at various scan rates are illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0004">4e</a>. With the increase in scan rate, there is also an increase in capacitance contribution, further indicating that the pseudocapacitive storage partially contributes to the whole capacity, especially under high rates. To better figure out the effectiveness of the medium-entropy effect on ME-NMVTP, the density of states (DOS) of ME-NMVTP, LE-NMVP, and LE-NMTP were calculated by using the density functional theory (DFT) method in the Materials Studio, which is based on the crystal structure model shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a> (Supporting Information). The total DOS diagrams in&nbsp;Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0004">4f–h</a> reveal higher electron conductivity of ME-NMVTP compared with LE-NMVP and LE-NMTP, as a certain electronic state appears near the Fermi level. Therefore, the electrons in ME-NMVTP are more easily excited from the valence band to conduction band.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0048_R_d148834726e1356" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Small">48</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0049_R_d148834726e1356" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Nano Energy">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Or more accurately, the decreased band/energy gaps for ME-NMVTP are attributed to the synergistic effect of the hybridized Mn 3d, V 3d, and Ti 3d orbitals, which is the key to distinguishing them from the LE-cathodes. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a> (Supporting Information) illustrates the electronic configuration of three TM ions, wherein unpaired electrons contribute to enhanced conductivity while their interaction leads to diverse local structures.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0050_R_d148834726e1364" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Adv. Energy Mater.">50</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0051_R_d148834726e1364" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - J. Alloys Compd.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Because the unpaired 3d orbital electrons in TMs can exert a significant influence on both adjacent Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion and density of states distribution. Moreover, diverse local structures can more easily accommodate local changes during sodium storage, effectively inhibiting the occurrence of phase transitions (discussed later).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0052_R_d148834726e1372" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In brief, the DOS simulations are consistent with the experimental results, which demonstrate the importance of the integrated/synergetic effects of Mn, V, and Ti to obtain ideal comprehensive performance.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202302046-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cf6e2756-d00a-48e6-8b07-8beef26bf5df/aenm202302046-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/cf6e2756-d00a-48e6-8b07-8beef26bf5df/aenm202302046-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ab28a938-807a-443c-92bd-69663ac227ca/aenm202302046-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/cf6e2756-d00a-48e6-8b07-8beef26bf5df/aenm202302046-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202302046-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202302046" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves of ME-NMVTP at sweep rates of 0.2–1.5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. b) The slope of the fitted line for the peak current (<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>) and the square root of scan rate (<i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>) at different sweep rates. c) GITT curves of ME-NMVTP and comparison of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients. Percentages of pseudocapacitive contribution for ME-NMVTP at d) 0.8&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> and e) all different sweep rates. f–h) Density of states of ME-NMVTP, LE-NMVP, and LE-NMTP.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The structure is an inherent factor that governs the properties of materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0053_R_d148834726e1413" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Chem. Rec.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As mentioned above, the unsatisfactory cycling performance of cathodes with multielectron redox reactions is primarily attributed to irreversible distortion in the crystal structure. For instance, previous studies have reported the origin of the rapid structural decay of LE-NMVP. Its pristine crystal structure cannot be fully recovered after one cycle, during that the cell parameters drastic changes and the corresponding shape of Mn/VO<sub>6</sub> octahedron constantly distorts.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0023_R_d148834726e1420" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Small Methods">23</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0024_R_d148834726e1420" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Mater.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To elucidate reinforced behavior for medium-entropy material in structural stability, the overall evolution of the ME-NMVTP crystal structure was observed by in situ XRD. The data were collected every 200 s at the rate of 20&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> in the 1st and 2nd GCD cycles. The diffraction peaks in the range of 15°–70°, including strong reflections such as (113), (211), (116), (300) and (226), are monitored to investigate the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction process (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0005">5a</a>). The full process can be divided into 2 regions (region I and II). As charging proceeds to the voltage of ≈3.4&nbsp;V, these peak reflections represented by (211) and (116), first shift rightward without other variation, indicating a gentle solid-solution reaction process. As Na-ions continue to extract and entered from the region I to II (3.4–4.3&nbsp;V), the disappearance of (211) peak (ii highlight) and the emergence of new reflections (iii highlight) suggest that ME-NMVTP undergoes biphasic reactions when entering the high voltage region. Subsequently, discharging to 1.5 from 4.3&nbsp;V, those new reflections gradually reduce and finally disappear, in the meanwhile, the (211) and (113) peaks shift back to the original position in an almost symmetrical way. The high reversibility (including peak intensity and angle) of the ME-NMVTP crystal lattice during the charging and discharging process was affirmed by the corresponding contour plot of in situ XRD (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0005">5b</a>). Normally, the high voltage window will cause the conventional low-entropy cathodes to occur adverse crystal distortion, which inevitably leads to mechanical damage to the crystal structure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0023_R_d148834726e1440" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Small Methods">23</a>, <a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0025_R_d148834726e1440" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Interestingly, the electrodes at 4.3 and 1.5&nbsp;V show the same space group (trigonal R-3c phase), which is beneficial for the stability maintained by the electrodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0028_R_d148834726e1445" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Sci.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The details of crystallographic data are listed in Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> (Supporting Information). Thus, compared to low-entropy cathodes, the combined effects of the multi-redox centers of the medium-entropy material effectively inhibits the undesirable distortion in the high voltage range. This hypothesis is further accessed by analyzing the lattice parameter variation of the ME-NMVTP at different electrochemical states. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0005">5e</a>, the volume change of the ME-NMVTP electrode was calculated as 7%, indicative of the stability of the lattice framework, which undertakes a low-strain operation during the electrochemical process. Such a small cell variation and reversible structure evolution should account for the superior cycling durability of ME-NMVTP. In brief, the thermodynamic medium-entropy effect can elevate the solid solubility of diverse TM species in one phase, promote compatibility among TM species with disparate sizes, and thereby impede large phase transition and lattice variation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0054_R_d148834726e1460" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - ACS Mater. Lett.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Taking advantage of the fact that different elements have different properties, the combination and interaction between elements make the ME-materials show a superposition effect and even a synergistic effect in terms of electrochemical performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0055_R_d148834726e1465" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Nat. Energy">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Consequently, the ME-NMVTP exhibits highly reversible multi-sodium storage characteristics even when charged to a high voltage of 4.5&nbsp;V. Based on the XRD characterization and Equation <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> (Supporting Information), the reaction mechanism of the multi-sodium storage procedure in ME-NMVTP is displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0005">5f</a>. At the stage of initial charging, 1.7 Na<sup>+</sup> extract from ME-NMVTP framework. Upon subsequent cycling in the voltage range of 1.5–4.3&nbsp;V, 2.7 Na<sup>+</sup> reversibly insert into and extract from the ME-NMVTP. Or rather, the pristine ME-NMVTP contains 3.0 Na, which is located at Na1 and Na2 sites. When it was initially charged to the Na-deficient phase (Na<sub>1.3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>V<sub>2/3</sub>Ti<sub>2/3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, ME-Na<sub>1.3</sub>), the most of Na<sup>+</sup> extract from the Na2 sites. For the fully discharged Na-rich phase (Na<sub>4</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>V<sub>2/3</sub>Ti<sub>2/3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, ME-Na<sub>4.0</sub>), Na<sup>+</sup> partially insert into the Na1 and Na2 sites, thus increasing their occupancy coefficient. While the extra Na<sup>+</sup> enters a new Na3 site, which is generated by the Coulombic repulsion caused by adjacent Na<sup>+</sup> at Na1 and Na2 sites.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0015_R_d148834726e1520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202302046-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/75537334-0a70-487d-8633-c39d7d0c6127/aenm202302046-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/75537334-0a70-487d-8633-c39d7d0c6127/aenm202302046-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/74333e25-53d3-4921-acb0-ff692fa05bef/aenm202302046-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/75537334-0a70-487d-8633-c39d7d0c6127/aenm202302046-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202302046-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202302046" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) In situ XRD patterns of ME-NMVTP cathode recorded during the 1st and 2nd cycles at 20&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> between 1.5 and 4.3&nbsp;V. b) Corresponding contour plot of the typical diffraction peaks. Rietveld refinement of the XRD pattern of ME-NMVTP cathode at c) 4.3&nbsp;V and d) 1.5&nbsp;V. e) The variation of cell parameters of ME-NMVTP cathode during the first cycle. f) Schematic structural change of ME-NMVTP during charge/discharge.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Evaluation of full-cell devices is essential to demonstrate the potential of ME-NMVTP in practical application. Thus, the full cells were assembled using ME-NMVTP and commercial hard carbon (HC) as the cathode and anode, respectively, denoted as HC//ME-NMVTP, and its working principle is given in the schematic diagram (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0006">6a</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0056_R_d148834726e1556" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Small">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The sodium storage behaviors of ME-NMVTP and HC in half cells are simply observed by GCD curves (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0006">6b</a>). Due to the large specific capacity difference, the loading of active substances for the cathode is supposed to be improved to balance the capacity in the full cell.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302046-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302046-bib-0057_R_d148834726e1565" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Adv. Energy Mater.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Note that the HC anode has undergone a pre-sodiation process to reduce its irreversible capacity before assembling the full cell. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0006">6c</a> shows the typical GCD curve of HC//ME-NMVTP at 10&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, with the same trend of ME-NMVTP cathode. Based on the mass of cathode active materials, its discharge capacity is 135.3&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> with an average voltage of 3.29&nbsp;V, corresponding to an energy density of 393.7&nbsp;W h kg<sup>−1</sup>. The slight decrease in voltage plateau is mainly related to the relatively high potential in the slope region of HC anode. The assembled HC//ME-NMVTP shows an initial discharge capacity of 73.5&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 500&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, which can well power a customized LED bulb (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0006">6d</a>). Moreover, after 1000 cycles, a high capacity retention rate of 82.3% is achieved. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202302046-fig-0006">6e</a> exhibits the rate performance of the HC//ME-NMVTP from 10 to 1000&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, and the initial Coulombic efficiency reached about 92.7% at 10&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>. Even at 1000&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, its discharge capacity can still maintain 80.7&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. The inset is the GCD curves at different rates, manifesting its superior high-rate capability. These full-cell configurations are sufficient to demonstrate that ME-NMVTP cathode is feasible for future industrial applications. However, the electrochemical properties of full cells should be further improved via the optimization of anode, electrolyte, assembly process, and so on. For instance, the electrochemical properties of the commercial HC in the voltage range of 0.01–2.0&nbsp;V are presented in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a> (Supporting Information), indicating much poorer cycling stability in comparison with the ME-NMVTP cathode.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202302046-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/abe13d4b-6f66-4dd4-bd28-3d1d8575f45e/aenm202302046-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/abe13d4b-6f66-4dd4-bd28-3d1d8575f45e/aenm202302046-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/abdf9391-3fb0-4dcc-a82e-a0635fb9a5b1/aenm202302046-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/abe13d4b-6f66-4dd4-bd28-3d1d8575f45e/aenm202302046-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202302046-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202302046" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic diagram of HC//ME-NMVTP SIFCs. b) GCD curves of the ME-NMVTP cathode and HC anode. c) GCD curves of HC//ME-NMVTP SIFCs. d) Cycling performance and e) rate performance of HC//ME-NMVTP SIFCs, insets are the picture of LED panel powered by HC//ME-NMVTP SIFCs and GCD curves at different current densities.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202302046-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202302046-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>A medium-entropy effect was first applied for designing advanced NASICON-type cathodes for SIBs. The as-prepared ME-NMVTP could achieve 2.7 electrons redox reaction per formula and maintain high reversibility even at high voltages up to 4.3&nbsp;V. Compared to low-entropy cathodes, the optimized ME-NMVTP with multiple redox couples exhibited excellent electrochemical performances, e.g., high specific capacity (147.9&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>), superior high-rate capability (57.7&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 5000&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>) and long cycling life (88.3% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 500&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>). Experimental characterizations and first-principles calculation revealed that the significantly enhanced performances are attributed to the more favorable kinetics properties and stable crystal structure. Furthermore, when coupled with the HC anode, the HC//ME-NMVTP delivered a high energy density of 393.7&nbsp;W h kg<sup>−1</sup> based on the cathode mass, proving the application feasibility of ME-NMVTP. Constructing a medium-entropy structure by regulating composition with substitution multi-metal ions can greatly stabilize the host framework of NASICON structure and solve the reversibility issues induced by the activation of more redox couples.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
